   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Dental, alveolar and postalveolar lateral approximants
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">

      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/w/index.php?title=Alveolar_lateral_approximant&amp;redirect=no" title="Alveolar lateral approximant">

      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>

        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Dental lateral approximant
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           l̪
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        alveolar lateral approximant
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in some
       <a href="/wiki/Speech" title="Speech">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
        alveolar
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
        postalveolar
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
        lateral
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
        approximants
       </a>
       is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        l
       </span>
       ⟩, and the equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <span class="monospaced" style="font-family: monospace, monospace;">
        l
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       As a
       <a href="/wiki/Sonorant" title="Sonorant">
        sonorant
       </a>
       , lateral approximants are nearly always voiced.
       <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_lateral_approximants" title="Voiceless dental, alveolar and postalveolar lateral approximants">
        Voiceless lateral approximants
       </a>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l̥/
       </span>
       are common in
       <a href="/wiki/Sino-Tibetan_languages" title="Sino-Tibetan languages">
        Sino-Tibetan languages
       </a>
       , but uncommon elsewhere. In such cases, voicing typically starts about halfway through the hold of the consonant. No language is known to contrast such a sound with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_lateral_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolar lateral fricative">
        voiceless alveolar lateral fricative
       </a>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [ɬ]
       </span>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In a number of languages, including most varieties of English, the phoneme
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l/
       </span>
       becomes
       <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">
        velarized
       </a>
       in certain contexts, a sound often called "
       <a href="#dark_l">
        dark l
       </a>
       ". Some languages, like many North American dialects of English, may not have a "clear"
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /l/
       </span>
       at all, or use it only before
       <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">
        front vowels
       </a>
       (especially
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">
         i
        </a>
        ]
       </span>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

          <span class="toctext">
           Bibliography
          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
       </ul>
      </div>
      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_lateral_approximants&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced alveolar lateral approximant:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
         approximant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by narrowing the vocal tract at the place of articulation, but not enough to produce a
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulent airstream
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        There are four specific variants of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [l]
        </span>
        :
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
           Dental
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the upper
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teeth" title="Teeth">
           teeth
          </a>
          , termed respectively
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
            apical
           </a>
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
            laminal
           </a>
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Denti-alveolar_consonant" title="Denti-alveolar consonant">
           Denti-alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with the blade of the tongue at the
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
           alveolar ridge
          </a>
          , and the tip of the tongue behind upper teeth.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
           Alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           apical
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           laminal
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
           Postalveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue behind the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           apical
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           laminal
          </i>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         lateral consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream over the sides of the tongue, rather than down the middle.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence">
        Occurrence
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_lateral_approximants&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Occurrence">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Languages may have clear apical or laminal alveolars, laminal denti-alveolars (such as French), or true dentals, which are uncommon. However, a true dental generally occurs allophonically before
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /θ/
       </span>
       in languages that have it, as in English
       <i>
        hea
        <b>
         l
        </b>
        th
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dental_or_denti-alveolar">

         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /l/
         </span>

           <a href="/wiki/File:Velarized_alveolar_lateral_approximant.ogg" title="File:Velarized alveolar lateral approximant.ogg">
            source
           </a>
           <span style="font-weight:bold;">
            ·
           </span>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
            help
           </a>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        velarized alveolar lateral approximant
       </b>
       (
       <b>
        dark
        <i>
         l
        </i>
       </b>
       ) is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound used in some
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . It is an alveolar, denti-alveolar, or dental lateral approximant, with a
       <a href="/wiki/Secondary_articulation" title="Secondary articulation">
        secondary articulation
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">
        velarization
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">
        pharyngealization
       </a>
       . The regular symbols in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represent this sound are ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        lˠ
       </span>
       ⟩ (for a velarized lateral) and ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        lˤ
       </span>
       ⟩ (for a pharyngealized lateral), though the dedicated letter ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɫ
       </span>
       ⟩, which covers both velarization and pharyngealization, is perhaps more common. The last symbol should never be confused with ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɬ
       </span>
       ⟩, which represents the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_lateral_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolar lateral fricative">
        voiceless alveolar lateral fricative
       </a>
       . However, some scholars
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       use that symbol to represent the velarized alveolar lateral approximant anyway – such usage is considered non-standard.
      </p>
      <p>
       If the sound is dental or denti-alveolar, one could use a
       <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
        dental
       </a>
       diacritic to indicate so: ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        l̪ˠ
       </span>
       ⟩, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        l̪ˤ
       </span>
       ⟩, ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɫ̪
       </span>
       ⟩.
      </p>
      <p>
       Velarization and pharyngealization are generally associated with more dental articulations of coronal consonants so dark l tends to be dental or denti-alveolar while clear l tends to be retracted to an alveolar position.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20054_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20054-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features_2">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_lateral_approximants&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Features of the dark l:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">
         approximant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by narrowing the vocal tract at the place of articulation, but not enough to produce a
        <a href="/wiki/Turbulence" title="Turbulence">
         turbulent airstream
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        There are four specific variants of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [ɫ]
        </span>
        :
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Dental_consonant" title="Dental consonant">
           Dental
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue at the upper
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teeth" title="Teeth">
           teeth
          </a>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Denti-alveolar_consonant" title="Denti-alveolar consonant">
           Denti-alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with the blade of the tongue at the
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_ridge" title="Alveolar ridge">
           alveolar ridge
          </a>
          , and the tip of the tongue behind upper teeth.
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Alveolar_consonant" title="Alveolar consonant">
           Alveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or, more rarely,
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20054_47-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20054-47">
            [47]
           </a>
          </sup>
          the blade of the tongue at the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">
            apical
           </a>
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">
            laminal
           </a>
          </i>
          .
         </li>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Postalveolar_consonant" title="Postalveolar consonant">
           Postalveolar
          </a>
          , which means it is articulated with either the tip or the blade of the tongue behind the alveolar ridge, termed respectively
          <i>
           apical
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           laminal
          </i>
          .
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li>
        It has a
        <a href="/wiki/Secondary_articulation" title="Secondary articulation">
         secondary articulation
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">
         velarization
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">
         pharyngealization
        </a>
        , meaning that the back or
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue#Structure" title="Tongue">
         root of the tongue
        </a>
        approaches the
        <a href="/wiki/Soft_palate" title="Soft palate">
         soft palate
        </a>
        (velum), or the back of the throat, respectively.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is an
        <a href="/wiki/Oral_consonant" title="Oral consonant">
         oral consonant
        </a>
        , which means air is allowed to escape through the mouth only.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         lateral consonant
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by directing the airstream over the sides of the tongue, rather than down the middle.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">
          Dutch
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         Standard
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinsMees200358,_197,_222_59-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinsMees200358,_197,_222-59">
           [59]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="nl">
           <a href="/wiki/Dutch_orthography" title="Dutch orthography">
            <i>
             ma
             <b>
              ll
             </b>
             en
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ˈmɑɫ̻ə]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'molds'
        </td>
        <td>
         Laminal; pharyngealized in northern accents, velarized or post-palatalised in southern accents. It is an allophone of
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /l/
         </span>
         before consonants and pauses, and also prevocalically when after the open back vowels
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ɔ, ɑ/
         </span>
         . Many northern speakers realize the final
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /l/
         </span>
         as a strongly pharyngealised vocoid
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ɤˤ]
         </span>
         , whereas some Standard
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Belgian_Dutch" title="Belgian Dutch">
          Belgian
         </a>
         speakers use the clear
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /l/
         </span>
         in all positions.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECollinsMees200358,_197,_222_59-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECollinsMees200358,_197,_222-59">
           [59]
          </a>
         </sup>
         See
         <a href="/wiki/Dutch_phonology" title="Dutch phonology">
          Dutch phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>

         /
         <i>
          <span lang="sh">
           <a href="/wiki/Gaj%27s_Latin_alphabet" title="Gaj's Latin alphabet">
            <i>
             <b>
              l
             </b>
             ak
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [ɫâ̠k]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'easy'
        </td>
        <td>
         Apical; may be syllabic; contrasts with
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /
          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
           ʎ
          </a>
          /
         </span>
         . See
         <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian_phonology" title="Serbo-Croatian phonology">
          Serbo-Croatian phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">
          Uzbek
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESjoberg196313_11-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESjoberg196313-11">
           [11]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          [
          <i>
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:AUDIENCE" title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
            <span title="Wikipedia:AUDIENCE">
             example needed
            </span>
           </a>
          </i>
          ]
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
        </td>
        <td>
         Apical; between a non-front rounded vowel and a consonant or
         <a href="/wiki/Juncture" title="Juncture">
          juncture
         </a>
         phoneme. Non-velarized denti-alveolar elsewhere.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESjoberg196313_11-3">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESjoberg196313-11">
           [11]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Variable_2">
        Variable
        <span id="Portuguese_dark_l">
        </span>
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_lateral_approximants&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Variable">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2">
         Language
        </th>
        <th>
         Word
        </th>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          IPA
         </a>
        </th>
        <th>
         Meaning
        </th>
        <th>
         Notes
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="3">
         <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
          Portuguese
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/European_Portuguese" title="European Portuguese">
          European
         </a>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECruz-Ferreira199593_64-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECruz-Ferreira199593-64">
           [64]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="pt">
           <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">
            <i>
             mi
             <b>
              l
             </b>
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [miɫ̪]
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         'thousand'
        </td>
        <td rowspan="3">
         When
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [lˠ ~ lʶ ~ lˤ ~ lˀ]
         </span>
         ,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
          <a href="#cite_note-65">
           [65]
          </a>
         </sup>
         most often dental.
         <a href="/wiki/Syllable#Coda" title="Syllable">
          Coda
         </a>
         is now
         <a href="/wiki/L-vocalization" title="L-vocalization">
          vocalized
         </a>
         to
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           <a href="/wiki/Voiced_labio-velar_approximant" title="Voiced labio-velar approximant">
            u̯
           </a>
          </span>
          ~
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           <a href="/wiki/Near-close_near-back_rounded_vowel" title="Near-close near-back rounded vowel">
            ʊ̯
           </a>
          </span>
          ]
         </span>
         in most of Brazil (as in rural parts of
         <a href="/wiki/Viana_do_Castelo_District" title="Viana do Castelo District">
          Alto Minho
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">
          Madeira
         </a>
         ).
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
          <a href="#cite_note-66">
           [66]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Stigmatized realizations such as
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
            ɾ
           </a>
          </span>
          ~
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_flap" title="Retroflex flap">
            ɽ
           </a>
          </span>
          ~
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_approximant" title="Retroflex approximant">
            ɻ
           </a>
          </span>
          ]
         </span>
         , the
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          /ʁ/
         </span>
         range,
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Palatal_approximant#Palatal" title="Palatal approximant">
           j
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         and even
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [∅]
         </span>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Zero_(linguistics)" title="Zero (linguistics)">
          zero
         </a>
         ) are some other coda allophones typical of Brazil.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
          <a href="#cite_note-67">
           [67]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Can be always dental and always dark (especially before back/rounded and close/unrounded vowels) in most dialects. See
         <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_phonology" title="Portuguese phonology">
          Portuguese phonology
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Most dialects
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
          <a href="#cite_note-68">
           [68]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <span lang="pt">
           <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">
            <i>
             <b>
              L
             </b>
             ituânia
            </i>
           </a>
          </span>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td align="center">
         <span class="nounderlines nowrap">
          <span class="unicode haudio">
           <span class="fn">
            <span style="white-space:nowrap">
             <a href="/wiki/File:Pt-br-litu%C3%A2nia.ogg" title="About this sound">
              <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
             </a>
            </span>
            <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/82/Pt-br-litu%C3%A2nia.ogg" title="Pt-br-lituânia.ogg">
             <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
              [ɫ̪it̪uˈɐ̃ɲ̟ɐ]
             </span>
            </a>
           </span>
           <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
            (
            <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              help
             </span>
            </a>
            ·
            <a href="/wiki/File:Pt-br-litu%C3%A2nia.ogg" title="File:Pt-br-lituânia.ogg">
             <span style="cursor:help;">
              info
             </span>
            </a>
            )
           </small>
          </span>
         </span>
        </td>
        <td>
         '
         <a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">
          Lithuania
         </a>
         '
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         Older and conservative

         </a>

        <td>
         '
